                        cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Prussian Blue Analogs as Battery Materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hurlbutt, Kevin; Wheeler, Samuel; Capone, Isaac; Pasta, Mauro</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Joule</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Cell Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue analogs have significant promise as active materials for the next generation of battery electrodes with improved cycle life and rate capability.  Their useful electrochem. properties include two independent redox centers per unit cell; a nanoporous, open framework for rapid ion conduction; high stability during ion (de)insertion; and structural and electrochem. tunability for diverse applications.  Here we share insights into how control of the five main crystallog. features (two transition-metal ions, the inserting ion, defects, and water) imparts control over the ion-insertion reaction.  We then identify five key opportunities to expand our understanding of these materials, including the role of water in their ion conduction, modeling, synthesis methods, use as anode materials, and technoeconomics.  Further research in these areas will accelerate the development of new, high-performing battery electrodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref9" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1021/ja510347s"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiao, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wray, L.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel air-stable sodium iron hexacyanoferrate (R-Na1.92Fe[Fe(CN)6]) with rhombohedral structure is demonstrated to be a scalable, low-cost cathode material for sodium-ion batteries exhibiting high capacity, long cycle life, and good rate capability.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium iron hexacyanoferrate with high Na content as a Na-rich cathode material for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">You, Ya; Yu, Xiqian; Yin, Yaxia; Nam, Kyung-Wan; Guo, Yu-Guo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Owing to the worldwide abundance and low-cost of Na, room-temp. Na-ion batteries are emerging as attractive energy storage systems for large-scale grids.  Increasing the Na content in cathode materials is one of the effective ways to achieve high energy d.  Prussian blue and its analogs (PBAs) are promising Na-rich cathode materials since they can theor. store two Na+ ions per formula unit.  However, increasing the Na content in PBAs cathode materials remains a major challenge.  Here we show that sodium iron hexacyanoferrate with high Na content can be obtained by simply controlling the reducing agent and reaction atm. during synthesis.  The Na content can reach as high as 1.63 per formula, which is the highest value for sodium iron hexacyanoferrate.  This Na-rich sodium iron hexacyanoferrate demonstrates a high specific capacity of 150 mAh·g-1 and remarkable cycling performance with 90% capacity retention after 200 cycles.  Furthermore, the Na intercalation/de-intercalation mechanism has been systematically studied by in situ Raman spectroscopy, X-ray diffraction and X-ray absorption spectroscopy anal. for the first time.  The Na-rich sodium iron hexacyanoferrate can function as a plenteous Na reservoir and has great potential as a cathode material for practical Na-ion batteries.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The urgent market demand of energy storage and conversion has promoted the extensive investigations of coordination polymers.  As a kind of simple cyano-bridged coordination polymers, Prussian blue (PB) and Prussian blue analogs (PBAs) have been considered as the promising cathode materials in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) because of their 3D open framework, adjustable structure and chem. compn.  Currently, the fundamental research and com. exploration of PB and PBAs in nonaqueousSIBs are making robust progress.  This review summarizes the recent advance and systematical cognitionof PB and PBAs, mainly discussing the chem. compn. and structure, material synthesis, modifica-tion strategy and sodium storage mechanism in nonaq. SIBs.  The structure-properties relationshipof PB and PBAs is deeply revealed from the respects of bulk phase and interfacial stability.  Moreover, theissues and perspectives are also analyzed to promote the future scientific research and com. appli-cation for PB and PBAs cathode in nonaq. SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref17" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.12.121"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, X.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improved cycling performance of Prussian Blue cathode for sodium ion batteries by controlling operation voltage range</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Xiaomin; Yang, Yang; Liu, Ershuai; Sun, Liqi; Wang, Hong; Liao, Xiao-Zhen; He, Yushi; Ma, Zi-Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">225</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">235-242</span>CODEN:

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue and its analogs were intensively studied as potential electrode materials for Na ion batteries.  A prussian blue sample was prepd. by a simple pptn. method and the electrochem. performance of the prussian blue (PB) cathode was studied at various temps. and in different voltage ranges.  When cycled in the voltage range of 2.0-4.0 V vs. Na/Na+, the PB cathode exhibited initial discharge capacities of 135.4 mAh g-1 (55°), 128.5 mAh g-1 (25°) and 99.2 mAh g-1 (-10°) at 10 mA g-1.  The PB cathode showed good cycling stability at low temp., however the cycling capacity degraded remarkably at elevated temp.  CV test indicated that the capacity fade was mainly due to the side reactions on the electrode-electrolyte interface at ∼4.0 V vs. Na/Na+.  XPS and FTIR analyses revealed several types of compds. formed on the cathode surface which indicated the complexity of the side reactions.  Controlling the high cut-off voltage at 3.8 V vs. Na/Na+ significantly improved the cycling stability of the PB electrode.  The PB cathode delivered 1C rate reversible capacity of 100.0 mAh g-1 in 2.0-3.8 V vs. Na/Na+ with outstanding capacity retention of 98.2% after 300 cycles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref18" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.04.067"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X. Through the inhibitor and temp. control, the border-rich structure was obtained, which provides a good contact between electrode-electrolyte interfaces and increases the transmission path for Na+ ions.  In addn., the as-prepd. sample with rhombohedral phase demonstrated lower band gap and lower energy barrier for Na+ ions insertion.  Benefiting from the kinetics optimization, the as-prepd. electrode exhibited initial capacity of 120 mA h g-1 and maintained nearly 80% after 280 cycles at c.d. of 100 mA g-1.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">First-Principles Study of Alkali and Alkaline Earth Ion Intercalation in Iron Hexacyanoferrate: The Important Role of Ionic Radius</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ling, Chen; Chen, Jiajun; Mizuno, Fuminori</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hexacyanoferrate compds. recently have attracted much interest because of their potential as aq. and nonaq. battery cathodes in the application of large-scale energy storage.  Here, the feasibility to use Fe hexacyanoferrate, Fe[Fe(CN)6], as a cathode candidate for nonaq. rechargeable batteries is assessed with 1st-principle calcns.  The structural deformation induced by the intercalation of alkali (Li+, Na+, K+, Rb+, Cs+) and alk. earth (Mg2+, Ca2+, Sr2+, Ba2+) ions into Fe-[Fe-(CN)6] induces is negligible as compared to other Li-ion battery cathodes.  The intercalation is strongly affected by the ionic radius of inserted species.  With increasing ionic size, the most stable interstitial site changes from face-centered site to body-centered site.  More importantly, the voltages for the intercalation are correlated to the ionic radius of the inserted species.  The insertion of cations with larger ionic radius happens at higher voltages, and thus provides higher energy d.  However, the intercalation of larger cations may also suffer from slower migration kinetics.  Thus, it is important to choose inserted cation with appropriate ionic size to achieve the optimized performance.  Overall, the results suggest hexacyanoferrate compds. are promising cathode materials for various types of nonaq. rechargeable batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref22" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.01.012"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Miao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium Storage in Na-Rich NaxFeFe(CN)6 Nanocubes</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">386</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">393</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ice-Assisted Synthesis of Highly Crystallized Prussian Blue Analogues for All-Climate and Long-Calendar-Life Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>22</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">3</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1302</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1310</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.nanolett.1c04492</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D22%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D1302-1310%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26issue%3D3%26author%3DJ.%2BPeng%26author%3DW.%2BZhang%26author%3DZ.%2BHu%26author%3DL.%2BZhao%26author%3DC.%2BWu%26author%3DG.%2BPeleckis%26author%3DQ.%2BGu%26author%3DJ.%2BZ.%2BWang%26author%3DH.%2BK.%2BLiu%26author%3DS.%2BX.%2BDou%26author%3DS.%2BChou%26title%3DIce-Assisted%2BSynthesis%2Bof%2BHighly%2BCrystallized%2BPrussian%2BBlue%2BAnalogues%2Bfor%2BAll-Climate%2Band%2BLong-Calendar-Life%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.nanolett.1c04492&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c14973&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.1c04492&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ice-Assisted Synthesis of Highly Crystallized Prussian Blue Analogues for All-Climate and Long-Calendar-Life Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Peng, Jian; Zhang, Wang; Hu, Zhe; Zhao, Lingfei; Wu, Can; Peleckis, Germanas; Gu, Qinfen; Wang, Jia-Zhao; Liu, Hua Kun; Dou, Shi Xue; Chou, Shulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">22</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1302-1310</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">For practical sodium-ion batteries, both high electrochem. performance and cost efficiency of the electrode materials are considered as two key parameters.  Prussian blue analogs (PBAs) are broadly recognized as promising cathode materials due to their low cost, high theor. capacity, and cycling stability, although they suffer from low-crystallinity-induced performance deterioration.  Herein, a facile "ice-assisted" strategy is presented to prep. highly crystd. PBAs without any additives.  By suppressing structure defects, the cathode exhibits a high capacity of 123 mAh g-1 with initial Coulombic efficiency of 87.2%, a long cycling lifespan of 3000 cycles, and significantly enhanced high/low temp. performance and calendar life.  Remarkably, the low structure distortion and high sodium diffusion coeff. have been identified via in situ synchrotron powder diffraction and first-principles calcns., while its thermal stability has been analyzed by in situ heated X-ray powder diffraction.  We believe the results could pave the way to the low-cost and large-scale application of PBAs in all-climate sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref27" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1007/s40820-021-00742-z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wan, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Post-Synthetic and In Situ Vacancy Repairing of Iron Hexacyanoferrate Toward Highly Stable Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nano-Micro Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">1</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">9</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1007/s40820-021-00742-z</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D14%26publication_year%3D2022%26journal%3DNano-Micro%2BLett.%26issue%3D1%26author%3DM.%2BWan%26author%3DR.%2BZeng%26author%3DJ.%2BMeng%26author%3DZ.%2BCheng%26author%3DW.%2BChen%26author%3DJ.%2BPeng%26author%3DW.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BHuang%26title%3DPost-Synthetic%2Band%2BIn%2BSitu%2BVacancy%2BRepairing%2Bof%2BIron%2BHexacyanoferrate%2BToward%2BHighly%2BStable%2BCathodes%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1007%252Fs40820-021-00742-z&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c14973&amp;doiOfLink=10.1007%2Fs40820-021-00742-z&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                10.1021/cm504091z</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D27%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D1997-2003%26journal%3DChem.%2BMater.%26issue%3D6%26author%3DW.%2BJ.%2BLi%26author%3DS.%2BL.%2BChou%26author%3DJ.%2BZ.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BM.%2BKang%26author%3DJ.%2BL.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DQ.%2BF.%2BGu%26author%3DH.%2BK.%2BLiu%26author%3DS.%2BX.%2BDou%26title%3DFacile%2BMethod%2Bto%2BSynthesize%2BNa-Enriched%2BNa1%252BxFeFe%2528CN%25296%2BFrameworks%2Bas%2BCathode%2Bwith%2BSuperior%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformance%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fcm504091z&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c14973&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fcm504091z&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile Method To Synthesize Na-Enriched Na1+xFeFe(CN)6 Frameworks as Cathode with Superior Electrochemical Performance for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Wei-Jie; Chou, Shu-Lei; Wang, Jia-Zhao; Kang, Yong-Mook; Wang, Jian-Li; Liu, Yong; Gu, Qin-Fen; Liu, Hua-Kun; Dou, Shi-Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1997-2003</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Different Na-enriched Na1+xFeFe(CN)6 samples can be synthesized by a facile one-step method, utilizing Na4Fe(CN)6 as the precursor in a different concn. of NaCl soln.  As-prepd. samples were characterized by a combination of synchrotron X-ray powder diffraction (S-XRD), Mossbauer spectroscopy, Raman spectroscopy, magnetic measurements, thermogravimetric anal., XPS, and inductively coupled plasma anal.  The electrochem. results show that the Na1.56Fe[Fe(CN)6]·3.1H2O (PB-5) sample shows a high specific capacity of more than 100 mAh g-1 and excellent capacity retention of 97% over 400 cycles.  The details structural evolution during Na-ion insertion/extn. processes were also investigated via in situ synchrotron XRD.  Phase transition can be obsd. during the initial charge and discharge process.  The simple synthesis method, superior cycling stability, and cost-effectiveness make the Na-enriched Na1+xFe[Fe(CN)6] a promising cathode for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref30" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2021.131083"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.             This article references
            30 other publications.
        </p><ol id="rightTab-references" class="useLabel"><li id="rightTab-ref1"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref1" class="rightTabRefNumLink">1</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit1" data-doi="10.1039/c1ee01782a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ong, S. P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chevrier, V. L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hautier, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jain, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Moore, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ceder, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Voltage, Stability and Diffusion Barrier Differences between Sodium-Ion and Lithium-Ion Intercalation Materials</span>. <i>Energy Environ. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">9</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">3680</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3688</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c1ee01782a</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Voltage, stability and diffusion barrier differences between sodium-ion and lithium-ion intercalation materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ong, Shyue Ping; Chevrier, Vincent L.; Hautier, Geoffroy; Jain, Anubhav; Moore, Charles; Kim, Sangtae; Ma, Xiaohua; Ceder, Gerbrand</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3680-3688</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To evaluate the potential of Na-ion batteries, we contrast in this work the difference between Na-ion and Li-ion based intercalation chemistries in terms of three key battery properties-voltage, phase stability and diffusion barriers.  The compds. investigated comprise the layered AMO2 and AMS2 structures, the olivine and maricite AMPO4 structures, and the NASICON A3V2(PO4)3 structures.  The calcd. Na voltages for the compds. investigated are 0.18-0.57 V lower than that of the corresponding Li voltages, in agreement with previous exptl. data.  We believe the obsd. lower voltages for Na compds. are predominantly a cathodic effect related to the much smaller energy gain from inserting Na into the host structure compared to inserting Li.  We also found a relatively strong dependence of battery properties on structural features.  In general, the difference between the Na and Li voltage of the same structure, ΔVNa-Li, is less neg. for the maricite structures preferred by Na, and more neg. for the olivine structures preferred by Li.  The layered compds. have the most neg. ΔVNa-Li.  In terms of phase stability, we found that open structures, such as the layered and NASICON structures, that are better able to accommodate the larger Na+ ion generally have both Na and Li versions of the same compd.  For the close-packed AMPO4 structures, our results show that Na generally prefers the maricite structure, while Li prefers the olivine structure, in agreement with previous exptl. work.  We also found surprising evidence that the barriers for Na+ migration can potentially be lower than that for Li+ migration in the layered structures.  Overall, our findings indicate that Na-ion systems can be competitive with Li-ion systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201909530"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, C.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Cathode Choice for Commercialization of Sodium-Ion Batteries: Layered Transition Metal Oxides versus Prussian Blue Analogs</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>30</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">1909530</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.201909530</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The Cathode Choice for Commercialization of Sodium-Ion Batteries: Layered Transition Metal Oxides versus Prussian Blue Analogs</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Qiannan; Hu, Zhe; Chen, Mingzhe; Zou, Chao; Jin, Huile; Wang, Shun; Chou, Shu-Lei; Liu, Yong; Dou, Shi-Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">30</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1909530</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  With the unprecedentedly increasing demand for renewable and clean energy sources, the sodium-ion battery (SIB) is emerging as an alternative or complementary energy storage candidate to the present com. lithium-ion battery due to the abundance and low cost of sodium resources.  Layered transition metal oxides and Prussian blue analogs are reviewed in terms of their com. potential as cathode materials for SIBs.  The recent progress in research on their half cells and full cells for the ultimate application in SIBs are summarized. Na-based batteries include related battery concepts, such as Na-ion, all solid-state Na batteries, Na/O2 and Na/S, that differ in key components and in redox chem., and therefore result in sep. challenges and metrics. Prussian blue and its analogs (PBAs) are promising Na-rich cathode materials since they can theor. store two Na+ ions per formula unit.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue and its analogs were intensively studied as potential electrode materials for Na ion batteries.  A prussian blue sample was prepd. by a simple pptn. method and the electrochem. performance of the prussian blue (PB) cathode was studied at various temps. and in different voltage ranges.  When cycled in the voltage range of 2.0-4.0 V vs. Na/Na+, the PB cathode exhibited initial discharge capacities of 135.4 mAh g-1 (55°), 128.5 mAh g-1 (25°) and 99.2 mAh g-1 (-10°) at 10 mA g-1.  The PB cathode showed good cycling stability at low temp., however the cycling capacity degraded remarkably at elevated temp.  CV test indicated that the capacity fade was mainly due to the side reactions on the electrode-electrolyte interface at ∼4.0 V vs. Na/Na+.  XPS and FTIR analyses revealed several types of compds. formed on the cathode surface which indicated the complexity of the side reactions.  Controlling the high cut-off voltage at 3.8 V vs. Na/Na+ significantly improved the cycling stability of the PB electrode.  The PB cathode delivered 1C rate reversible capacity of 100.0 mAh g-1 in 2.0-3.8 V vs. Na/Na+ with outstanding capacity retention of 98.2% after 300 cycles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref18" class="rightTabRefNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit18" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.04.067"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The performance of a Prussian blue cathode is affected by its structure and stability. In addn., the as-prepd. sample with rhombohedral phase demonstrated lower band gap and lower energy barrier for Na+ ions insertion.  Benefiting from the kinetics optimization, the as-prepd. electrode exhibited initial capacity of 120 mA h g-1 and maintained nearly 80% after 280 cycles at c.d. of 100 mA g-1. The optimized passivation layer not only protects the electrode form the adverse side reactions at high voltage but also delivers low interface impedance.                         rightTab-cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">First-Principles Study of Alkali and Alkaline Earth Ion Intercalation in Iron Hexacyanoferrate: The Important Role of Ionic Radius</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ling, Chen; Chen, Jiajun; Mizuno, Fuminori</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hexacyanoferrate compds. recently have attracted much interest because of their potential as aq. and nonaq. battery cathodes in the application of large-scale energy storage.  Here, the feasibility to use Fe hexacyanoferrate, Fe[Fe(CN)6], as a cathode candidate for nonaq. rechargeable batteries is assessed with 1st-principle calcns.  The structural deformation induced by the intercalation of alkali (Li+, Na+, K+, Rb+, Cs+) and alk. earth (Mg2+, Ca2+, Sr2+, Ba2+) ions into Fe-[Fe-(CN)6] induces is negligible as compared to other Li-ion battery cathodes.  The intercalation is strongly affected by the ionic radius of inserted species.  With increasing ionic size, the most stable interstitial site changes from face-centered site to body-centered site.  More importantly, the voltages for the intercalation are correlated to the ionic radius of the inserted species.  The insertion of cations with larger ionic radius happens at higher voltages, and thus provides higher energy d.  However, the intercalation of larger cations may also suffer from slower migration kinetics.  Thus, it is important to choose inserted cation with appropriate ionic size to achieve the optimized performance.  Overall, the results suggest hexacyanoferrate compds. are promising cathode materials for various types of nonaq. rechargeable batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.01.012"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Miao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium Storage in Na-Rich NaxFeFe(CN)6 Nanocubes</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">386</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">393</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1021/cm504091z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W. J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S. L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J. Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, Y. M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J. L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, Q. F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H. K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S. X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile Method to Synthesize Na-Enriched Na1+xFeFe(CN)6 Frameworks as Cathode with Superior Electrochemical Performance for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>27</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">6</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1997</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2003</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/cm504091z</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile Method To Synthesize Na-Enriched Na1+xFeFe(CN)6 Frameworks as Cathode with Superior Electrochemical Performance for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Wei-Jie; Chou, Shu-Lei; Wang, Jia-Zhao; Kang, Yong-Mook; Wang, Jian-Li; Liu, Yong; Gu, Qin-Fen; Liu, Hua-Kun; Dou, Shi-Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1997-2003</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Different Na-enriched Na1+xFeFe(CN)6 samples can be synthesized by a facile one-step method, utilizing Na4Fe(CN)6 as the precursor in a different concn. of NaCl soln.  As-prepd. samples were characterized by a combination of synchrotron X-ray powder diffraction (S-XRD), Mossbauer spectroscopy, Raman spectroscopy, magnetic measurements, thermogravimetric anal., XPS, and inductively coupled plasma anal.  The electrochem. results show that the Na1.56Fe[Fe(CN)6]·3.1H2O (PB-5) sample shows a high specific capacity of more than 100 mAh g-1 and excellent capacity retention of 97% over 400 cycles.  The details structural evolution during Na-ion insertion/extn. processes were also investigated via in situ synchrotron XRD.  Phase transition can be obsd. during the initial charge and discharge process.  The simple synthesis method, superior cycling stability, and cost-effectiveness make the Na-enriched Na1+xFe[Fe(CN)6] a promising cathode for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2021.131083"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y. S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Solvent-Free Mechanochemical Synthesis of Na-Rich Prussian White Cathodes for High-Performance Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Eng. J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>428</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">2021</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">131083</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.cej.2021.131083</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i12">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.4c14973?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.4c14973</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Process of synthesizing PBAs, images of the synthesis process from PB to PW, Rietveld refinement results, d<i>Q</i>/d<i>V</i> curves of charge/discharge cycles, electrochemical impedance spectra of samples, <i>R</i><sub>S</sub>, <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub>, and <i>R</i><sub>CT</sub> values of each sample, ratio of the Fe valence according to the XPS peak area, and peak shifts of (200), (220), and (400) XRD peaks of each sample (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c14973/suppl_file/am4c14973_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c14973/suppl_file/am4c14973_si_001.pdf">am4c14973_si_001.pdf (919.29 kb)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="931885baba2f54b8-SJC">
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {
    const modalContainer = document.querySelector('.my-main-container');

    // Function to show the modal
    function showModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'flex';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'block';
    }

    // Function to hide the modal when the close button is clicked
    function hideModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'none';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'none';
    }

    // Hide the modal initially
    hideModal();

    // Function to handle clicks outside the modal
    function handleClickOutside(event) {
        // const modalContainer = document.querySelector(".my-main-container");
        // Check if the click target is not a child of the modal container
        if (!modalContainer.contains(event.target)) {
            hideModal();
        }
    }

    // Add a click event listener to the close button
    document
        .querySelector('.close-button')
        .addEventListener('click', hideModal);

    // Add a click event listener to the document to handle clicks outside the modal
    document.addEventListener('click', handleClickOutside);

    const screenHeight = window.innerHeight;
    function updateModalPosition() {
        const scrollY = window.scrollY;
        // console.log("scrollY= " + scrollY);
        // modalContainer.style.top = `${50 + scrollY}px`;
        modalContainer.style.top = `${scrollY + screenHeight / 2}px`;
        // console.log("new top= " + modalContainer.style.top);
    }

    // Update the modal position when the user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', updateModalPosition);

    // Initialize the modal position
    updateModalPosition();

    //---Cookie---
    // Function to set the cookie with a given name, value, and expiration time in days
    function setCookie(name, value, days) {
        var expires = '';
        if (days) {
            var date = new Date();
            date.setTime(date.getTime() + days * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000);
            expires = '; expires=' + date.toUTCString();
            console.log(expires + 'this is expires dateUTC');
        }
        document.cookie = name + '=' + (value || '') + expires + '; path=/';
        // console.log("document.cookie is: " + document.cookie);
    }

    if (!document.cookie.includes('modalAd')) {
        // Show Modal
        showModal();

        // Set the cookie with the name "modalAd", value "true", and expiration of 3 day
        setCookie('modalAd', 'true', 3);
    } else {
        hideModal();
    }
});

</script>

<script nonce="931885baba2f54b8-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

          //   console.log(event.target);
          //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
          //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
          //     $(this).off();
          //   }
          // });
          $("#gdpr-con-btn").click(function () {
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            hideForm();
          });
        }, time);
      }

      //Show the message
      function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();
      }

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
      }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;
          $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
      }

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

    $(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
  </script>
</p>
-->

                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="931885baba2f54b8-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>
